## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces, nonlinear damping, or parametric/external driving.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear damping plus restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (Mathieu-type parametric excitation)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (exact pendulum restoring torque)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) (mixed friction model, effectively sign(v))
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * x * v (mixed polynomial nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power terms in x (x²) in restoring force → asymmetric potential, symmetry-breaking behavior
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to x²·v → amplitude-dependent damping (van der Pol type self-excitation/limit cycles)
- Cubic velocity terms (v³) → Rayleigh-type nonlinear dissipation, energy-dependent damping rate
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) → external periodic driving or parametric modulation
- Product terms x·v → phase-space coupling, can indicate coordinate-dependent damping or Hamiltonian perturbation
- sin(c·x) replacing linear x → pendulum-like large-amplitude nonlinearity with bounded restoring force
- Time appearing only inside trigonometric functions → autonomous dynamics with periodic forcing rather than explicit time dependence

**GT:** `-1.1449635767559*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.445567501246416*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.10853689295113*sin(t)`

Key components of GT:
1. A term proportional to `x*exp(-|x|)`
2. A term proportional to `log(|v| + 1)` — since v ≤ 0 on this domain, `|v| = -v`, so this is `log(-v + 1)` or `log(1 - v)`
3. A term proportional to `sin(t)`

Let me analyze the basis functions needed:
- `x*exp(-|x|)`: This is an odd function of x that decays exponentially
- `log(|v| + 1)`: logarithmic in |v|
- `sin(t)`: simple sinusoidal in t

Now I'll check each candidate for the possibility of matching these three basis functions.

**Key observations for many candidates:**

Many candidates use `exp(c*sin(t+c))` for the time dependence. Can `c2*exp(c3*sin(c4*t + c5))` equal `A*sin(t) + const`? No — `exp(sin(t))` is not a sinusoidal function; it's a composition of exponential and sine, which produces a different periodic function. These are NOT equivalent to `sin(t)` plus a constant. So any candidate relying solely on `exp(sin(t))` for time dependence cannot match.

Similarly, `cos(c*sin(t+c))` is not equivalent to `sin(t)` plus a constant.

Many candidates use `v` (linear in v) instead of `log(|v|+1)`. Since v ≤ 0, `log(1-v)` is NOT linear in v. So `c*v` cannot match `log(|v|+1)`.

Many candidates use `x/(c+x²)` or `log(c*|x|+1)` or `log(c*exp(cx)+1)` or `sin(cx+c)` for the x-dependence. None of these equal `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Let me check `x/(c+x²)`: This is a rational function, while `x*exp(-|x|)` involves an exponential. Not equivalent.

`log(c*exp(cx)+1)`: This is a softplus-like function, not equivalent to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

`sin(cx+c)`: Periodic, while `x*exp(-|x|)` decays. Not equivalent.

`x*cos(ct)`: This has t-dependence in the x-coefficient. Not equivalent to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

`x/(c+x)`: Rational function, not equivalent to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

`log(c*|x|+1)`: Even function of x, while `x*exp(-|x|)` is odd. Not equivalent.

`x*exp(c*v)`: Depends on v, not equivalent to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Let me systematically go through all 50 candidates. For each, I need ALL THREE basis functions to be representable.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the term `x*exp(-|x|)` or any function that could be equivalent to it. The x-dependent terms available are: `x/(c+x²)`, `x/(c+x)`, `log(c*|x|+1)`, `log(c*exp(cx)+1)`, `sin(cx+c)`, `x*cos(ct)`, `x`, `x³`, `x*exp(cv)`, etc. None of these can represent `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Additionally, most candidates lack `log(|v|+1)` (using `v` linearly instead) and/or lack `sin(t)` (using `exp(sin(t))` or `cos(sin(t))` instead).

Going through all 50 candidates systematically, none can simultaneously represent all three required basis functions: `x*exp(-|x|)`, `log(|v|+1)`, and `sin(t)`.
